  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_bc76d20a-3d76-4d44-9462-7d48c93711f4'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText2080337605858180278" style="display:none">It's been three months since everyone under the age of fifteen became trapped in the bubble known as the FAYZ.<br /><br />Three months since all the adults disappeared. GONE.<br /><br />Food ran out weeks ago. Everyone is starving, but no one wants to figure out a solution. And each day, more and more kids are evolving, developing supernatural abilities that set them apart from the kids without powers. Tension rises and chaos is descending upon the town. It's the normal kids against the mutants. Each kid is out for himself, and even the good ones turn murderous.<br /><br />But a larger problem looms. The Darkness, a sinister creature that has lived buried deep in the hills, begins calling to some of the teens in the FAYZ. Calling to them, guiding them, manipulating them.<br /><br />The Darkness has awakened. And it is hungry.</span>

<div id="review_146031074" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/146031074" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/146031074?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781405251525" href="/book/show/6923670-hunger">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer146031074" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15294796941711581896"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Whilst this book impressed me greatly, as did the first of the series, I found that there were still those little things that majorly irked me, even amid the fast-paced sci-fi and action told in a gripping and imaginative way; it was these little things that again prevented me from awarding the novel the 5 stars it would have otherwise deserved.<br/><br/>So what's the problem?<br/>I can sum it up in two points:<br/>1) Sam is a lame protagonist.<br/>2) All the girls are 'cute'.<br/><br/>Let me explain.<br/><br/>Pointer number one: Sam i</span>
  <span id="freeText15294796941711581896" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Whilst this book impressed me greatly, as did the first of the series, I found that there were still those little things that majorly irked me, even amid the fast-paced sci-fi and action told in a gripping and imaginative way; it was these little things that again prevented me from awarding the novel the 5 stars it would have otherwise deserved.<br><br>So what's the problem?<br>I can sum it up in two points:<br>1) Sam is a lame protagonist.<br>2) All the girls are 'cute'.<br><br>Let me explain.<br><br>Pointer number one: Sam is one of those over the top do-gooders that just don't exist in real life, let alone at fifteen. He is given too much credit for his age by the author and his character becomes increasingly unrealistic, Sam is essentially the very ideal stereotype of the 'good guy', the hero, the constant martyr for the greater good. Oh please, he's a fifteen year old guy in a town with no adults, he should be drinking like a fish and raiding the porn sections at the local stores. His self-pitying attitude also results in generating absolutely zero sympathy.<br><br>Pointer number two: The girls of this novel are teeth-grindingly useless. Astrid the genius is Sam's 'beautiful' girlfriend and the dark and seductive Diana is Caine's obedient sidekick. Nearly all the females are trophies and repeatedly described as 'hot' or 'cute'. They also need protecting. There is way too much of this:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380345209i/699929.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And nowhere near enough of this:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380345209i/699930.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Whatever happened to the ass-kicking female? She isn't in this book. Other readers might point out characters like Brianna and Lana as examples of strong females. However, in the heat of battle when Brianna is required to be strong, she instead decides to run away and cook herself a pigeon. What the hell?? And Lana is not strong enough to defeat the lure of the 'Darkness' but rather leads the others into danger and needs to be rescued. By Sam, Caine and Duck (the male characters who come swooping in to rescue her), in fact. Also, most of the battle stuff is done man-to-man. Usually featuring Sam, Caine, Drake, Edilio, Orc and Jack; the girls tend to hide behind the rubble or are used to threaten their boyfriends (i.e. Caine threatening to kill Astrid unless Sam surrender). Seriously? Why are all the strongest mutants male, anyway? Is radiation that particular?<br><br>After this great big rant, you're gonna be thinking - how the hell did it get 4 stars then?<br><br>Well, it's a great story really. It's exciting and action-packed, there are always several sub-plots happening at once meaning that the book never gets slow or tiresome. Some of the characters are interesting and highly likeable and it's a good portrayal of growing up and the difficulties of being a teenager (only times by about a thousand). Every teenager should be reading this series, my only recommendation is that they follow it up with a large dose of Buffy The Vampire Slayer to remind themselves that having a vagina does not equal weak, pathetic damsel in distress. Quite the opposite at times.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15294796941711581896" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17655699115577774491">The Gone series is the type of series that has you marking down your calendars waiting for the next installment. Both Hunger, and its predecessor, Gone were gripping and fantastic. Hunger, while darker than Gone, really dove into deeper topics. The cast of the series is diverse in its variety, and you are free to pick your favorites. The dialogue, while nothing fantastic, is realistic and easy. Same as the writing. Yes, the writing has some grammatical mistakes and is far from lyrical, but it se</span>
  <span id="freeText17655699115577774491" style="display:none">The Gone series is the type of series that has you marking down your calendars waiting for the next installment. Both Hunger, and its predecessor, Gone were gripping and fantastic. Hunger, while darker than Gone, really dove into deeper topics. The cast of the series is diverse in its variety, and you are free to pick your favorites. The dialogue, while nothing fantastic, is realistic and easy. Same as the writing. Yes, the writing has some grammatical mistakes and is far from lyrical, but it serves its purpose. Great book that I recommend to all.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9832601856072787274">This was a YA dystopian story which followed on from Gone.<br/><br/>I felt sorry for Sam in this story, he had so much responsibility and little reward, and the fact that the other kids ignored him instead of helping him must have been frustrating.<br/><br/>The storyline in this was mainly about the kids all going hungry as the food ran out, and Sam trying to do something about it.   <span id="freeText9832601856072787274" style="display:none">This was a YA dystopian story which followed on from Gone.<br /><br />I felt sorry for Sam in this story, he had so much responsibility and little reward, and the fact that the other kids ignored him instead of helping him must have been frustrating.<br /><br />The storyline in this was mainly about the kids all going hungry as the food ran out, and Sam trying to do something about it. We had killer mutant worms in the fields, Caine trying to take over the power plant, and this weird entity called ‘the darkness’ playing a role too. This was an interesting story, but the pace was a bit slow in places. <br /><br />The ending to this was okay, and things did seem to be looking up a bit.<br />6.5 out of 10<br /></span>

<div id="review_54057074" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/54057074" />
    <a title="Nightfalltwen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/326509-nightfalltwen"><img alt="Nightfalltwen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539364895p2/326509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/54057074?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nightfalltwen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nightfalltwen" href="/user/show/326509-nightfalltwen">Nightfalltwen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/326509-nightfalltwen?shelf=teen">teen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer54057074&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer54057074" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15971955840846878799">I will leave a better review after I sleep, it's 1:30am and I just couldn't stop until I had finished.<br/><br/>********<br/><br/>Well. Now that I've had time to sleep, given my contacts a chance to thoroughly soak and really given myself a chance to absorb that which I gobbled down last night, I must say that I am completely happy with the fact that I didn't wait until the paperback version came out. The hardcover might be more expensive, but it was totally, <i>totally</i> worth it in the end.<br/><br/>So Hunger takes place 3 mont</span>
  <span id="freeText15971955840846878799" style="display:none">I will leave a better review after I sleep, it's 1:30am and I just couldn't stop until I had finished.<br /><br />********<br /><br />Well. Now that I've had time to sleep, given my contacts a chance to thoroughly soak and really given myself a chance to absorb that which I gobbled down last night, I must say that I am completely happy with the fact that I didn't wait until the paperback version came out. The hardcover might be more expensive, but it was totally, <i>totally</i> worth it in the end.<br /><br />So Hunger takes place 3 months after the FAYZ came into being. Kids are literally starving and no one is helping out. Kids are being, well, kids. Lazy and waiting for someone to just hand them food on a silver platter.<br /><br />I adore Sam. My heart goes completely out to this fictional character. As he says during an argument, he's just <i>fifteen</i> and everyone is expecting him to be the dad. It's so much pressure and he's so very real because all he wants is pizza and a chance to make out with his girlfriend. He's so adult and yet so child-like at the same time. He doesn't want to make the decisions but everyone keeps coming to him for answers that he doesn't have.<br /><br />And it breaks him.<br /><br />My complete and most utter compliments to Michael Grant. The scene with Astrid and Sam in the dark where he finally unloads and breaks down got to me. I wanted to reach through the pages and clutch the poor kid to my bosom and tell him it was going to be alright. Of course I have no idea if it <i>is</i> going to be alright, but I wanted to give him some sort of assurance that he is not a failure and he's doing the best that he can and that's a very good thing.<br /><br />There was another scene that got to be. Like <i>really</i> got to me. When they're about to execute Hunter. It reminded me of The Handmaid's Tale where the Handmaidens are encouraged to execute by pulling a rope to hang someone. The entire basis of that scene was to show just how a crowd will degenerate if they are hungry enough. The promise of food is a strong, <i>strong</i> motivator.<br /><br />I have to say that this reminded me of a quote that I read in a Reader's Digest a very long time ago:<br /><br /><i>"Literature duplicates the experience of living in a way that nothing else can, drawing you so fully into another life that you temporarily forget you have one of your own. That is why you read it, and might even sit up in bed till dawn, throwing your whole tomorrow out of whack, simply to find out what happens to some people -- you know perfectly well -- are made up."</i> -Barbara Kingslover<br /><br />I ran a gauntlet of emotions while reading this book. I stayed up far too late. I bit my nails. I couldn't sit still. And <i>that</i> is what made this such an astounding book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15971955840846878799" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7606335796087634669" style="display:none"><u>HUNGER</u> is an amazing story because of the realistic characters, the spectacular <br /><br />details put into the setting, and the way it shows the theme of accepting hard <br /><br />responsibilities.. Some people may say that this novel is unrealistic, or too built on the <br /><br />theme of finding weakness in others, but it shows taking on responsibility, even if it is <br /><br />unwanted. <br /><br />Sam Temple is one of the well crated characters in this book. He is a <br /><br />fifteen year old boy who is forced to become a leader of hundreds of kids, after every <br /><br />adult and teen ages fifteen and up in his town disappeared. He is overwhelmed with <br /><br />responsibilities like finding a way to feed every kid with food supply decreasing, and <br /><br />protecting people from the upcoming gangs. He is like any other teenager in this world. <br /><br />Readers can connect to him and eventually, feel what he feels. What distinguishes Sam <br /><br />from some other kids in his town are his powers. Right before the FAYZ, the time <br /><br />when the adults disappeared, many kids began to discover that they <br /><br />had unnatural powers like no one else. Sam’s unique power was light. Not only could he <br /><br />create his own light but he could fire beams of heated light that could be used as a <br /><br />defense, or a weapon. <br /><br />The detail written about the setting and plot of this book is amazing. Its like <br /><br />reading a movie! There’s action, romance, and the threat of life or death. The setting is <br /><br />described in a way that makes the reader feel like the action can be happening in their <br /><br />own city or town. It is a page turning book that makes you not want the story to end. <br /><br />How many people have been given a tough responsibility to handle? In this <br /><br />novel, Sam Temple and everyone else is faced with almost too many tasks to fulfill. He <br /><br />has to prevent arising gang violence, avoid being killed by his twin brother, <br /><br /><br />This amazingly written novel is praised for its life like characters, the extremely <br /><br />detailed setting, and the theme of accepting difficult responsibilities. By the end of the <br /><br />story you will feel what the characters feel and wish there were more of the story to read. <br /><br />Everyone at some point in their lives has to take on. Everyone has seen, heard about or <br /><br />been through bullying </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer56651803" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10534913938262914153">Oh my god. I just finished reading "Hunger", and I devoured all 590 pages in less than 24 hours. So I basically just used an entire Sunday to read the book. Definetly one of my better Sundays.<br/><br/>"Hunger" is about... well, it's about a lot of things, but basically it all started in "Gone", the first book in the series, when all the people over the age of fourteen dissapeared. Just poof. Vanished. Gone. And so, all of the kids at the age of fourteen and younger are left to fend for themselves. Not a </span>
  <span id="freeText10534913938262914153" style="display:none">Oh my god. I just finished reading "Hunger", and I devoured all 590 pages in less than 24 hours. So I basically just used an entire Sunday to read the book. Definetly one of my better Sundays.<br /><br />"Hunger" is about... well, it's about a lot of things, but basically it all started in "Gone", the first book in the series, when all the people over the age of fourteen dissapeared. Just poof. Vanished. Gone. And so, all of the kids at the age of fourteen and younger are left to fend for themselves. Not a pretty sight at all. There is just so much going on in this novel, I can't wrap my mind around it. There's hunger and starvation with food running out. There's a fight between kids with powers and kids without them. There's torture and mind games. There's love and revenge. Even eating disorders. And worst of all, there's a lurking darkness in the midst of all the horrible drama. And the darkness is hungry.<br /><br />If you have to read one book during the entire summer, read "Gone". Then, right after you're done with Gone, read "Hunger". Oh wait, I said one book... well whatever, just read the series! It's amazing, mind-blowing, phenomonal, just pure writing at it's best. Michael Grant is a huge talent and I'm surprised that he's just getting discovered. The only bad thing is waiting to see what happens next. Now I'm hungry... for the next book in the series!</span>

<div id="review_40782818" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40782818" />
    <a title="Karin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/72729-karin"><img alt="Karin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464658459p2/72729.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/40782818?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karin" href="/user/show/72729-karin">Karin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/72729-karin?shelf=youngadult">youngadult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/72729-karin?shelf=2008-reads">2008-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/72729-karin?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer40782818" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13334845288968186916">Things aren’t getting any easier in the FAYZ (Fall-out Alley Youth Zone) since the big Thanksgiving Battle against Caine and the other Coates Academy kids. In fact, everything seems to be going from bad to worse. Sam, the appointed leader of Perdido Beach, is feeling the pressure of all the day to day decisions. The biggest problem that everyone is facing is starvation. With the fear and confusion that followed the disappearance of everyone 15 and over, the kids that were left did what they want</span>
  <span id="freeText13334845288968186916" style="display:none">Things aren’t getting any easier in the FAYZ (Fall-out Alley Youth Zone) since the big Thanksgiving Battle against Caine and the other Coates Academy kids. In fact, everything seems to be going from bad to worse. Sam, the appointed leader of Perdido Beach, is feeling the pressure of all the day to day decisions. The biggest problem that everyone is facing is starvation. With the fear and confusion that followed the disappearance of everyone 15 and over, the kids that were left did what they wanted - including eating what they wanted. Nothing was done to preserve food for the future, so meats and vegetables went bad, leaving food in short supply. The kids in Perdido Beach and Coates Academy are left eating what canned food is left. One day it might be asparagus for breakfast, wax beans for lunch, and hot dog relish for dinner. No one is in good spirits and when Caine recovers from his encounter with The Darkness and makes another move for power, things only get worse.<br /><br />Sam is suffering from all the stress, Little Pete’s powers are getting scarier every day, some of the kids that haven’t developed powers are beginning to start trouble, and important people are switching sides. Danger is at its all time high. Death seems imminent. <br /><br />Michael Grant has produced a very satisfying sequel. The tension and excitement in the story is palpable. Character development continues to be a strong point. The new characters that are introduced add to the plot, but our favorites from GONE continue to play a large role in the story. HUNGER is the second book in a six-part series. Michael Grant is currently working on the third which will be titled LIES. HUNGER will be released June 2009, but be sure to read GONE first, you’ll need the backstory to really appreciate the sequel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13334845288968186916" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_109760719" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/109760719" />
    <a title="Amelia, free market Puritan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan"><img alt="Amelia, free market Puritan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508223427p2/1852293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/109760719?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amelia, free market Puritan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amelia, free market Puritan" href="/user/show/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan">Amelia, free market Puritan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=ya-kids-teen">ya-kids-teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=series-books">series-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer109760719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6535499686226173544"><b>Pretty good! Though not as good as GONE: too many different plots and points of view made this book kind of hectic.</b><br/><br/>Michael Grant is definitely an author with a knack for action-driven stories heavy on suspense and excitement. <i>Gone</i> was a great beginning book for the series: it established the problem (all growups "poof" out and leave kids to fend for themselves) and dealt with the power struggles that ensued between the townies and the dysfunctional delinquents over at Coates. <i>Hunger</i> was therefor</span>
  <span id="freeText6535499686226173544" style="display:none"><b>Pretty good! Though not as good as GONE: too many different plots and points of view made this book kind of hectic.</b><br /><br />Michael Grant is definitely an author with a knack for action-driven stories heavy on suspense and excitement. <i>Gone</i> was a great beginning book for the series: it established the problem (all growups "poof" out and leave kids to fend for themselves) and dealt with the power struggles that ensued between the townies and the dysfunctional delinquents over at Coates. <i>Hunger</i> was therefore able to go more in-depth on the problems of the FAYZ: three months have gone by, and supplies and food are drastically depleted. What was so cool about this book was that - while I was reading it - I forgot that I was reading a fictional sci-fi/fantasy thriller. I was so wrapped up in "oh my gosh! what are they going to DO?!" and really feeling all the agitation and the anxiety that the characters felt. I read this 500+ page thing in 2 days, lordy lord! That's pretty good for me! I seriously could not put it down. <br /><br />The (main) characters are all so incredibly dynamic. Just wanna give a quick shout-out to Dekka - I absolutely love her "go get'em tiger" personality. SHE needs to lead the FAYZ! Sam/Astrid and Caine/Diana went together very nicely - when I found myself annoyed at Sam and Astrid (and unfortunately, I did at times) I had Caine and Diana to balance the story out. Most of the main characters are portrayed in Hi-Def and so it made it incredibly easy to relate to them - the good guys and the not-so-good guys - and really care about what was going on with them. I personally find it really interesting that Grant has created an antagonist, Caine (cause technically that's what he is) that I actually care about. Maybe Caine's not <i>bad</i> enough - that's more like Drake - but I really enjoyed his scenes. He's such a megalomaniac, but perhaps a misunderstood megalomaniac? <br />I will say, though, that characterization and plot, two things that Grant knows how to handle really well, got a little hectic in this installment. I *do* like the large ensemble cast of characters, BUT in this story, I think there were a little <i>too many</i> perspectives, too many characters to keep track of, and I think that sometimes scenes that really should have gone to the "main characters" (like Sam and Astrid) were spent on all these secondary characters. That's okay and everything, except that I frequently found myself not quite understanding why Sam, Astrid or Lana would do certain things. Also, if Sam and Astrid just got together at the end of <i>Gone</i>, it seems a little early (to me) for them to already be having problems. But then again, they didn't have very many scenes together, and the few scenes they did have together they spent bickering. Maybe the spotlight will be on them a little more in <i>Lies</i>. All I'm saying is that because the perspective was off them, I didn't really feel as connected to them as I did in the first book. Astrid in particular started to annoy me a bit. She's supposed to be a genius, so I found it odd that she was so hostile to Albert's economic ideas. If you're so smart, Astrid, why can't you see that it's a good thing to try and rebuild the economy? Maybe we should start referring to "Astrid the Genius" as "Astrid the Commie." Just kidding! Caine and Diana, though, were great. They did get their bit of spotlight.<br />The same characterization notice also applied to the plots, here. I think there were so many things going on in this particular installment, that they just didn't seem fully covered. There's a major food shortage in the FAYZ. Caine and gang are trying to make a big for power again. The Darkness wants to be fed. Something's up with Petey. Albert wants to keep the flame of capitalism alive. Lots of really cool plot points that didn't really seem to get an even amount of coverage. It's totally cool to have different things going on, but toward the end, things just seemed rushed.<br />But anyway, another awesome installment to a new favorite series. I can't wait to get my hands on <i>Lies</i>. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6535499686226173544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3946292057098176982"><b>-- 2017 --</b><br/>Ook bij het herlezen bleef <i>Hunger</i> spannend. Ik houd van de manier waarop Michael Grant een wereld vol diverse en realistische personages weet neer te zetten. Elk personage heeft een goed uitgewerkt achtergrondverhaal en het is fantastisch om ze allemaal beter te leren kennen. Ook de manier waarop nieuwe personages zoals Orsay en Duck aan het verhaal worden toegevoegd voelt heel natuurlijk. En duizend hartjes voor Little Pete natuurlijk! Ik blijf fan van deze boeken!<br/><br/><b>-- 2014 --</b><br/>I really e</span>
  <span id="freeText3946292057098176982" style="display:none"><b>-- 2017 --</b><br />Ook bij het herlezen bleef <i>Hunger</i> spannend. Ik houd van de manier waarop Michael Grant een wereld vol diverse en realistische personages weet neer te zetten. Elk personage heeft een goed uitgewerkt achtergrondverhaal en het is fantastisch om ze allemaal beter te leren kennen. Ook de manier waarop nieuwe personages zoals Orsay en Duck aan het verhaal worden toegevoegd voelt heel natuurlijk. En duizend hartjes voor Little Pete natuurlijk! Ik blijf fan van deze boeken!<br /><br /><b>-- 2014 --</b><br />I really enjoyed reading <b>Hunger</b>. I was afraid I wouldn't like it as much as I liked <i>Gone</i> but fortunately it was as awesome as the first book in this series. <br />Even with all the strange paranormal powers, I feel like this book is realistic; I imagine a world like grown ups would be like this. All the fighting, the hungry kids, it was kind of scary but realistic in my opinion.<br />I thought the writing style was amazing - it was impossible to put the book down. I can't wait to start with the next installment :D</span>

<div id="review_1261070374" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1261070374" />
    <a title="April (Aprilius Maximus)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20658145-april-aprilius-maximus"><img alt="April (Aprilius Maximus)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589331862p2/20658145.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1261070374?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="April (Aprilius Maximus)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="April (Aprilius Maximus)" href="/user/show/20658145-april-aprilius-maximus">April (Aprilius Maximus)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<div id="review_102220661" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/102220661" />
    <a title="Aaron Vincent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2924544-aaron-vincent"><img alt="Aaron Vincent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360133074p2/2924544.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/102220661?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aaron Vincent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aaron Vincent" href="/user/show/2924544-aaron-vincent">Aaron Vincent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2924544-aaron-vincent?shelf=dystocalypse">dystocalypse</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer102220661" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11663922096638384329">Someone told me that Hunger is not as great as Gone. But man, I think Hunger is waaaay better than Gone. I'm not saying I didn't like Gone but my complain about GONE before was that everything happens so fast and its almost like a blur. For Hunger, the action scenes are sharper and the plot is more solid. <br/><br/>Michael Grant did an amazing job creating intense parallel events. There's always a huge thing happening in one place, at the same time on another place and sometimes also in an another differe</span>
  <span id="freeText11663922096638384329" style="display:none">Someone told me that Hunger is not as great as Gone. But man, I think Hunger is waaaay better than Gone. I'm not saying I didn't like Gone but my complain about GONE before was that everything happens so fast and its almost like a blur. For Hunger, the action scenes are sharper and the plot is more solid. <br /><br />Michael Grant did an amazing job creating intense parallel events. There's always a huge thing happening in one place, at the same time on another place and sometimes also in an another different place. The action scenes are really non-stop that sometimes you have to stop reading and remind yourself to breath. <br /><br />The only problem I got while reading it was there is a freaking huge number of characters. And it was really confusing at first cause there are characters that has somehow a similar name like Brianna and Brittney, Harry, Hunter and Hank, etc.. There are just a lot of characters that I even made <i>
  <b>my own top ten favorite characters</b>
</i> for this particular book.(Posted <a href="http://aaronvincent.tumblr.com/post/606151663/my-top-ten-favorite-hunger-characters" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>).<br /><br />I guess the only weak point of the book is Sam and Astrid. They are too self-righteous and pretentious that at one point, they seem to be fake. Their romance is also weak, its too controlled and a little sappy. And for real Sammy boy,?? you are using "Babe" to call Astrid? How cheesier can that be.! Its a little evil but I somehow been glad when Astrid got hit and Sam was whipped. I think they deserve it to wake them up, step up their game and stop trying to be saints. Don't get me wrong, I sympathize Sam when he breaks down but he desperately needs to be a badass to redeem himself. I hope Michael Grant can redeem these two characters since they are the leads. <br /><br />I really loved this book and I am eager to read LIES that I just bought over the weekend. But somehow I think I need to read something else first so that I wouldn't get the impression that HUNGER and LIES are not the same thing. <br /><br />And boy oh boy! Chips, burgers and pizza tastes even better after reading Hunger. lol. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="11663922096638384329" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2091373058" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2091373058" />

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2091373058?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/26734926-emma">Emma</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781405251532" href="/book/show/7549252-hunger">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26734926-emma?shelf=teen-young-adult">teen-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26734926-emma?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2091373058" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2392922456770414250">Hunger is the second novel in a six book series, but doesn't suffer from "middle book syndrome" too badly. In the previous novel, we saw the immediate aftermath of an event that caused everyone over the age of 15 to simply disappear from an American town. Part Lost, part Misfits, part Lord of the Flies, the children had to setup their own survival system,while dealing with some of them developing superpowers, and dealing with mutations in their surroundings.<br/><br/>This sequal novel picks up a few month</span>
  <span id="freeText2392922456770414250" style="display:none">Hunger is the second novel in a six book series, but doesn't suffer from "middle book syndrome" too badly. In the previous novel, we saw the immediate aftermath of an event that caused everyone over the age of 15 to simply disappear from an American town. Part Lost, part Misfits, part Lord of the Flies, the children had to setup their own survival system,while dealing with some of them developing superpowers, and dealing with mutations in their surroundings.<br /><br />This sequal novel picks up a few months later when the real issues with having a contained, children run town kick in- mainly food shortages, rivalries, and workshy children. The main drama comes from the continued war with a separate group of children, led by a sadistic leader.<br /><br />I'm continuing to enjoy this series and will continue onto number 3.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_190280872" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/190280872" />
    <a title="Lexie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5889376-lexie"><img alt="Lexie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339363563p2/5889376.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/190280872?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lexie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lexie" href="/user/show/5889376-lexie">Lexie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5889376-lexie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5889376-lexie?shelf=kick-ass-mc">kick-ass-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5889376-lexie?shelf=awesome-side-characters">awesome-side-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5889376-lexie?shelf=great-concept">great-concept</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer190280872" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11873748015150642077">First off, let me say that I am writing this at 3 in the morning. Please forgive any grammar mistakes or lack of coherency.<br/><br/><br/>Okay, so this was a reread. I like rereading books that I've enjoyed, and I wanted to reread the first two before reading the next two in the series. Although it may be a while before I get to read those.<br/>Anyways.<br/>It went a lot slower for me, this time, than the first time. I'm not saying it wasn't gripping, exactly; once I'd start reading it again, I'd get hooked. But when I </span>
  <span id="freeText11873748015150642077" style="display:none">First off, let me say that I am writing this at 3 in the morning. Please forgive any grammar mistakes or lack of coherency.<br /><br /><br />Okay, so this was a reread. I like rereading books that I've enjoyed, and I wanted to reread the first two before reading the next two in the series. Although it may be a while before I get to read those.<br />Anyways.<br />It went a lot slower for me, this time, than the first time. I'm not saying it wasn't gripping, exactly; once I'd start reading it again, I'd get hooked. But when I had free time, when I could've easily picked it up and read, I didn't have the desire. It didn't pull at me.<br /><br />I really like the Gone series. It's an extremely unique idea; intriguing, powerful, intricate, horrifying, incredibly dark. Action and gore and power plays and war. So refreshing when compared to a lot of YA these days.<br />But the perspectives. Oh G-d, the perspectives. I missed a few on my one status update. There were not 18 perspectives. There were 21 perspectives. <br />Now I'm sorry, but that's just ridiculous. Yes, I realize that the majority of these perspectives were somewhat necessary, that they told important parts of the plot, but G-d . . . 21? I know there are at least a few he could easily have chopped without hurting the book. As it is, I'd find myself really getting into one person's POV, and then their section ends, and I don't get to read about them again for a few chapters. That was incredibly frustrating.<br />Then there are the characters themselves. Some of the characters I love. Caine, Diana, Lana, Orc, Edilio, Dekka, Duck. But some of the characters, some of the "good" characters, annoyed the shit out of me. Sam, our hero Sam. Sometimes I really liked him. Sometimes I wanted to punch him in the face. Astrid, the hero's girlfriend. She's supposed to be a genius, but honestly, most of the time I just see a stuck-up girl using big words. She did not appeal to me.<br />There were a few other characters I was a bit iffy on as well.<br />Also, I found an uncomfortable amount of typos. Editors, icu.<br /><br />That aside, it was a very, very good book. I'm so amazed at Grant's ability to construct these incredibly intricate plots and keep it all together, lead it all to a certain point, a fitting conclusion. Like I said before, it's so incredibly unique, and once I really got into the action, I couldn't tear myself away. Some have complained about Grant's very choppy, dramatic writing style, but I think it's absolutely perfect for these books. <br />My problems with the perspectives and characters left me unable to rate this a five star, but it is a very solid four star. I really like this series, and I would recommend it to anyone who enjoys dark, action-filled stories with sci-fi, mutations, and a lot of horror.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11873748015150642077" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=superheroes-or-superpowers">superheroes-or-superpowers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=nightmare-fuel">nightmare-fuel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=mental-illness-or-disability">mental-illness-or-disability</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1464184209" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4975868124725943378">And this is where the plot diverges from the paths of things like <i>Under the Dome</i> -- where that book lasted only about a week, <i>Hunger</i> jumps ahead three months into their isolated bubble, with no end in sight.<br/><br/>Which means depleting resources.<br/><br/>Which means the title of this book. <br/><br/>The kids are starving, literally dying from starvation unless they can manage to work together and cooperate and rebuild a sustainable society/economy. (Once again, this touches on my love of survival logistics and resource m</span>
  <span id="freeText4975868124725943378" style="display:none">And this is where the plot diverges from the paths of things like <i>Under the Dome</i> -- where that book lasted only about a week, <i>Hunger</i> jumps ahead three months into their isolated bubble, with no end in sight.<br /><br />Which means depleting resources.<br /><br />Which means the title of this book. <br /><br />The kids are starving, literally dying from starvation unless they can manage to work together and cooperate and rebuild a sustainable society/economy. (Once again, this touches on my love of survival logistics and resource management!! I blame a childhood growing up on strategy games like Warcraft/Age of Empires, plus city simulators. I seriously just love reading books where people have to fuss over the arguably banal details of survival and running a society.)<br /><br />But the title also applies to the Darkness' hunger, a motif that runs throughout the whole book as you slowly find out more about the malevolent presence haunting the town of Perdido Beach.<br /><br />There's also the weight of responsibility which piles and piles and piles on Sam's shoulders now, being the leader for 300+ kids that he never asked for. Again with my usual Animorphs comparisons: it took Jake much much much longer to crack and splinter under the strain , but it actually makes sense to me. Because Sam has <i>more</i> lives resting directly on his shoulders, more weird real-world logistical issues to sort out (how <i>do</i> you plant crops!?), and then <i>also</i> immature kids bringing him totally pointless problems &amp; petty disagreements as if he's their parent. I would want to dropkick some of those children into the Pacific ocean, tbh.<br /><br />Small sidebar: a scene in the <i>very first chapter</i> alone merits this book the "nightmare fuel" tag, because I have a serious thing about <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[worms burrowing into skin <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I can't deal. The exact same thing also happened in one of the earlier <i>Remnants</i> books, too, so hey, Mr. Grant, I'M ONTO YOU.<br /><br />And now that I'm two books in, I'm attached to the characters! Super-spoilery thoughts: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I was devastated when I thought Edilio was dead. His and Sam's found-brothers dynamic is so great in its complete, absolute trust and loyalty (<i>Don't die on me</i>--I'm actually starting to slash ship it, what is happening). Brianna is spunky and wonderful, and Dekka's a badass, and I love that she calls out straight white Sam for not having the same POV on othering that she does as a black lesbian. Astrid's relationship with her little brother remains complex &amp; interesting as always. <i>And Caine and Diana.</i> I love them I love them I need fic for them!! I ship it so hard! Also, Caine's grief &amp; about-turn &amp; helping them out at the end was fantastic; really, all I want from this series is a long-term redemption arc for him. It <i>feels</i> like that's what Grant is going for, so I'm excited to see where this goes.<br /><br />And fine, Quinn has now grown on me. I also really liked Lana's lil' monologue about the effect of the Gaiaphage on her, and gosh but my heart clenched at her dumb heroic attempt to take it down. They were such good character moments:<br /><blockquote>“I am Lana Arwen Lazar. My dad was into comic books, so he named me Lana for Superman’s girlfriend Lana Lang. And my mom added Arwen for the elf princess in The Lord of the Rings. And I never, ever do what I’m told.” </blockquote><br />LOVE. &lt;3 However, the narrative has a tendency to send her off on adventures by herself or sideline her for long periods, which means it's a bit harder to get a grasp on her too. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />And a few thoughts about the ending: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[DUUUUUUUUUUCK. :( I found myself stricken on the subway, wanting to cry about a minor character who I never expected to have that many Feelings over. His last moments, ugh. And the Big Bad is banished -- but surely the Gaiaphage will come back, though, right? It's too big of an ~endgame~ villain to waste, I feel like. Although with the buildup of the mutants v. normals tension and violence, and the next book being called <i>Lies</i>, I'm assuming their enemies in the next book will be themselves, and will be their population splitting into factions and tearing each other apart.<br /><br />My only quibble -- the thing preventing it from being a five-star book for me -- is that the characters got off pretty scott-free this time. All of the characters I had straight-up given up for dead -- Edilio, Dekka, Diana, Lana, even Sam, as I had a moment of thinking "man it would be a cool move to kill off the leader in the second book" -- were brought back, thanks to Lana's power. I feel like there should have been more consequences from the tumultuous climax; right now, the characters feel sheltered by the protective arm of the narrative, if that makes any sense? As in, to be truly <i>all bets are off!!!!</i>, I kind of wanted someone to die, even if it would have hurt my heart for it to happen. Confrontations without real in-universe risk of death aren't true confrontations at all. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I don't want to say that much about the book outside of the cut-tags, because, again, spoilers! But I liked this one a lot. I've already bought the next book, and had to restrain myself from diving right into it (and distracting myself with some fluffy dragon fantasy instead). This is turning out to be a solid dystopian YA series (<i>with superpowers</i>), with really gritty visceral violence and the struggles of running a nascent society built on the backs of wastrel youths... and best of all, a premise that isn't your cut-and-dried autocratic dystopia with plucky anti-government rebellion.<br /><br />Favourite quotes:<br /><blockquote>
  <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[  Sam stood paralyzed for a few seconds, just a few seconds—but later in memory it would seem so long. Too long.<br /><br />***<br /><br />  “Why are we here? This is Mose’s cottage.”<br />  “Because you’re too dangerous. No one at Coates wants you around until you get a grip on yourself.”<br />  He blinked at another returning memory. “I hurt someone.”<br />  “You thought Chunk was some kind of monster. You were yelling a word. Gaiaphage. Then you smacked Chunk through a wall.”<br />  “Is he okay?”<br />  “Caine. In the movies a guy can get knocked through a wall and get up like it’s no big deal. This wasn’t a movie. The wall was brick. Chunk looked like roadkill. Like when a raccoon gets run over and over and over and keeps getting run over for a couple of days.”<br /><br />***<br /><br />  "Are you okay?”<br />  “Sure. Why not? This morning I was responsible for 332 people. Now I’m only responsible for 331. And part of me is almost thinking, okay, one less mouth to feed.”<br /><br />***<br /><br />  Someone was tugging at Mary’s shirt from behind. She looked around and with a sinking heart saw a little boy named . . . named . . . she couldn’t remember his name. But the second little boy behind him she remembered was Sean. She knew why they were there. They had both recently had their fifth birthdays. The age limit for the day care was four. At age five you had to move out—hopefully to a house with some responsible older kids.<br />  “Hi, kids. What’s up?” Mary asked as she brought her face down to their level.<br />  “Um . . . ,” the first one said. And then he burst into tears.<br />  She shouldn’t do it, she knew she shouldn’t, but she couldn’t stop herself from putting her arms around the little boy. And then Sean started crying as well, so the embrace was extended, and John was in there, too, and Mary heard herself saying of course, of course they could come back, just for today, just for a little while.<br /><br />***<br /><br />  COATES ACADEMY WAS quite a bit the worse for wear. Battles had damaged the façade of the main building. There was a hole in the whitewashed brick so big, you could see an entire second-story classroom, a cross-section of the floor beneath it, and a jagged gap that didn’t quite reach to the top of the first-story window below. Most of the glass in the windows was gone. The kids had made an effort to keep the elements out by duct-taping sheets of plastic over the holes, but the tape had loosened and now the plastic and the tape hung limp, stirring with the occasional breeze. The building looked as if it had been through a war. It had been.<br /><br />***<br /><br />  Sam tried to sleep. Wanted desperately to sleep.<br />  He was in the spare bedroom at Astrid and Mary and John’s house. In the dark. On his back. Staring up at the ceiling.<br />  Downstairs, in the kitchen, there were a half dozen cans of food. He was hungry. But he had had his ration for the day. He had to set the example.<br />  Still, he was hungry, and the hunger didn’t care about setting an example.<br />  Food downstairs. And Astrid down the hall.<br />  A different kind of hunger, that. And there, too, he had to set a good example.<br />  I am nothing but good examples, he told himself gloomily.<br /><br />***<br /><br />  “What am I supposed to do? Tell three hundred kids spread out in seventy or eighty different homes that they can’t watch DVDs? Confiscate iPods?”<br />  “It’s not easy playing daddy to three hundred kids,” Astrid admitted.<br />  “I’m not anyone’s daddy,” Sam practically snarled. Another sleepless night, in a long string of them, had left him in a foul mood. “I’m supposed to be the mayor, not the father.”<br />  “These kids don’t know the difference,” Astrid pointed out. “They need parents. So they look to you. And Mother Mary. Me, even, to some extent.”<br />  Little Pete chose that moment to begin floating in the air. Just lifted off a foot, eighteen inches, hovered there, his arms floating, toes pointed downward.<br />  Sam noticed immediately. Astrid didn’t.<br />  “What the—”<br /><br />***<br /><br />  Astrid started to say something, but stopped herself. She took a couple of calming breaths. Then, in a more measured tone, she said, “Sam, I figured you had enough on your shoulders. I’m worried about you.”<br />  He dropped his hands to his sides. His voice dropped as well. “I’m fine.”<br />  “No, you’re not,” Astrid said. “You don’t sleep. You never have a minute to yourself. You act like everything that goes wrong is your fault. You’re worried.”<br />  “Yeah, I’m worried,” he said. “Last night we had a kid who killed and ate a cat. The whole time he’s telling me about it he’s weeping. He’s sobbing. He used to have a cat himself. He likes cats. But he was so hungry, he grabbed it and . . .”<br />  Sam had to stop. He bit his lip and tried to shake off the despair that swept over him. “Astrid, we’re losing. We’re losing. Everyone is . . .” He looked at her and felt tears threaten. “How long before we have kids doing worse than killing cats?”<br />  When Astrid didn’t answer, Sam said, “Yeah, so I’m worried.<br /><br />***<br /><br />  “You know, we should have hung out more, back in the old days,” Howard said to Albert.<br />  “You didn’t know I existed, back in the old days,” Albert said.<br />  “What? Come on, man. There’s, like, a dozen brothers in the whole school and I didn’t notice one?”<br />  “We’re the same shade, Howard. That doesn’t make us friends,” Albert said coolly.<br />  Howard laughed. “Yeah, you were always a grind. Reading too much. Thinking too much. Not having much fun. Good little family boy, make your momma proud. Now look at you: you’re a big man in the FAYZ.”<br />  Albert ignored that. He wasn’t interested in reminiscing. Not with Howard, for sure, not really with anyone. The old world was dead and gone. Albert was all about the future.<br /><br />***<br /><br />  Lana lay her hand against the gruesome hole.<br />  “Don’t want no more rock,” Orc repeated.<br />  The bleeding stopped almost immediately.<br />  “Does it hurt?” Lana asked. “I mean the rock. I know the hole hurts.”<br />  “No. It don’t hurt.” Orc slammed his fist against his opposite arm, hard enough that any human arm would have been shattered. “I barely feel it. Even Drake’s whip, when we was fighting, I barely felt it.”<br />  Suddenly he was weeping. Tears rolled from human eyes onto cheeks of flesh and pebbles. “I don’t feel nothing except . . .” He pointed a thick stone finger at the flesh of his face.<br />  “Yeah,” Lana said. Her irritation was gone. Her burden was smaller, maybe, than Orc’s.<br />  Lana pulled her hand away to see the progress. The hole was smaller. Still crusted with blood, but no longer actively bleeding.<br />  She put her hand back in place. “Just a couple minutes more, Orc.”<br />  “My name’s Charles,” Orc said.<br />  “Is it?”<br />  “It is,” Howard confirmed.<br />[...] “What were you guys doing going into the worm field?” Lana asked.<br />  Howard shot a resentful look at Albert, who answered, “Orc was picking cabbage.”<br />  “My name’s Charles Merriman,” Orc repeated. “People should call me by my real name sometimes.”<br /><br />***<br /><br />  “I have nightmares,” he said. “The battle. You know. The big battle.”<br />  “You were really brave. You saved those kids in the day care.”<br />  “Not all of them,” Quinn said shortly. He fell silent for a moment, back in the dream. “There was this coyote. And this kid, right? And . . . and . . . Okay, so I could have shot him, maybe, a little sooner, right? But I was scared of hitting the kid. I was so scared I’d hit that little kid, so I didn’t shoot. And then it was, like, too late. You know?”<br />  Lana nodded. She didn’t show any sympathy, and strangely Quinn thought that was a good thing because if it wasn’t you, and <i>you</i> hadn’t been there, and <i>you</i> hadn’t been holding a machine gun with your finger frozen on the trigger, and <i>you</i> hadn’t heard your voice coming out of your throat in a scream like an open artery, and <i>you</i> hadn’t seen what he had seen, then you didn’t have a right to be sympathetic because you didn’t understand anything. You didn’t understand anything.<br />  Anything.<br />  Lana just nodded and put her palm against his heart and said, “I can’t heal that.”<br /><br />***<br /><br />  “Diana will give me Jack,” Caine said. “And then we will turn off the lights and feed the—” He stopped very abruptly. He blinked in confusion.<br />  “Feed?” Drake echoed, puzzled.<br />  Caine almost didn’t hear him. His brain seemed to trip, to skip a step, like a scratch in a DVD when the picture pixilates for a moment before starting up again. The familiar grounds of Coates Academy swam before his eyes.<br />  <i>Feed?</i><br />  What had he meant?<br />  <i>Who</i> had he meant?<br />  “You can all go,” he said, distracted.<br /><br />***<br /><br />  It felt like someone had a rope wrapped around his brain. Someone he couldn’t see, someone standing far off in the dark, invisible. The rope disappeared into gloom and mystery, but at this end it was attached to him.<br />  And out there, the Darkness held the other end. Yanked it whenever it liked.<br />  Like Caine was a fish on a hook.<br /><br />***<br /><br />  Edilio looked at the shocked faces of the kids around him. He had been seconds away from impatiently ordering them into the field. Most wearing sneakers. None with experience seeing what the zekes looked like.<br />  He’d been one hesitation away from ordering forty-nine kids to their deaths.<br />  “Get back on the bus,” Edilio said shakily. “Get back on the bus.”<br />  “What about lunch?” someone asked.<br /><br />***<br /><br />  She went out into the night looking for a kid who was very strong—and, she hoped, very weak.<br /><br />***<br /><br />  Dekka watched him go. “Edilio’s a good guy,” she said.<br />   “But?”<br />  “But, he’s a normal.”<br />  “There aren’t going to be lines like that, between freak and normal,” Sam said firmly.<br />  Dekka almost, but didn’t quite, laugh. “Sam, that’s a great concept. And maybe you believe it. But I’m black and I’m a lesbian, so let me tell you: From what I know? Personal experience? There are always lines.”<br /><br />***<br /><br />  The memories of the battle—those couldn’t even be called memories because weren’t memories something from the past? That day might have happened three months ago, but it wasn’t the past to Quinn, it was right here, right now, always. Like a parallel life happening simultaneously with this life. He was driving through the night and feeling the gun buck buck buck in his hands and seeing the coyotes and the kids, all mixed up together, all crisscrossing, weaving through the arcs of the bullets.<br /><br />***<br /><br />  The crowd was dead quiet now. Of course they were quiet, some still-functioning part of his mind thought bitterly, it’s entertaining watching someone melt down in public.<br /><br />***<br /><br />  “If there’s a God, I wonder if he’s sitting in the dark on the end of his bed wondering how he managed to screw everything up.”<br /><br />***<br /><br />  “And what are you, Astrid?” he shouted. “A smug know-it-all! You point your finger at me and say, ‘Hey, Sam, you make the decisions, and you take all the heat.’”<br />  “Oh, it’s my fault? No way. I didn’t anoint you.”<br />  “Yeah, you did, Astrid. You guilted me into it. You think I don’t know what you’re all about? You used me to protect Little Pete. You use me to get your way. You manipulate me anytime you feel like it.”<br /><br />***<br /><br />  He smiled, patted Drake’s gaunt cheek, and with a hint of his old swagger said, “We’re going to reshuffle the deck. Sam thinks he holds all the cards. But we’re going to change everything.”<br />  “We’re going to feed the monster who has his hooks in your head,” Diana said coldly. “Don’t try to dress it up. We’re feeding a monster and hoping it will show its gratitude by letting go of your leash.”<br />  “Let it go, Diana,” Caine said. The bluster was gone.<br />  Diana glanced to see that Drake was out of earshot. “Bug’s not coming back. You know that.”<br />  Caine chewed at his thumb. Jack had the unsettling thought that he might be hungry enough to eat his own finger.<br />  “You don’t know that,” Caine said. “He might have had trouble finding Orsay. He wouldn’t turn against me.”<br />  “No one’s loyal to you, Caine,” Diana said. “Drake is itching to take you down. No one at Coates is rushing to bail you out. You only have one person who actually cares about you.”<br />  “You?”<br />  Diana didn’t answer. “I know it has a hold on you, Caine. I’ve seen it. But that monster of yours isn’t loyal to you, either. It will use you and throw you away. It will be everything and you will be nothing.”<br /><br />***<br /><br />  “I’m going to deal with Caine. I have to stop him here.”<br />  “You don’t want to go at Caine and Drake by yourself,” Edilio objected. “No way. I’m not letting you kill yourself.”<br />  Sam forced a laugh. “I wouldn’t dream of it. Howard, as soon as you get to town, find Breeze if you don’t pass her on the way. If you don’t find Brianna, find Taylor. Tell them to send help. And tell them I need someone to let me know what’s going on with you guys at the mine.”<br />  “Maybe should have turned on the phones, huh?” Edilio said. He winced, realizing too late that it sounded like sniping.<br />  Sam said, “Yeah. Add that to the list of mistakes I’ve made lately.”<br />  “Yeah, here’s one not to make, Sam: don’t go in there by yourself.”<br />  “Didn’t I just say I wouldn’t?” Sam said evenly.<br />  Edilio looked him in the eyes. Sam looked down and said, “But in case anything happens to me, you all take orders from Edilio.”<br />  Dekka nodded solemnly.<br />  “Do not do that to me,” Edilio said. “Do not die on me, Sam.”<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer572276736" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer3917161294529792901">3.5 stars. I thought this was an entertaining read, and coming off a couple heavier reads it was a nice break!<br/><br/>There were so many characters and plots going on during this one. I didn't really have a hard time keeping them all in line, I'm more worried about the ratio of meaningful review to crossing the line into a rambling review, but I'm going to try anyways!<br/><br/>First off, <b>Astrid and Sam</b>. As for their relationship, I still don't really believe it. This was something I had said for Gone and I still</span>
  <span id="freeText3917161294529792901" style="display:none">3.5 stars. I thought this was an entertaining read, and coming off a couple heavier reads it was a nice break!<br><br>There were so many characters and plots going on during this one. I didn't really have a hard time keeping them all in line, I'm more worried about the ratio of meaningful review to crossing the line into a rambling review, but I'm going to try anyways!<br><br>First off, <b>Astrid and Sam</b>. As for their relationship, I still don't really believe it. This was something I had said for Gone and I still say it here. They feel more like friends than anything romantic.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380415031i/818962.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Overall, I liked Astrid less in this book than in Gone. I'm not sure what it was about her, I just didn't really care about her. Sam was fine, I liked him as much as in Gone. He's definitely more at a breaking point, but I can't say I blame him!<br><br><b>Caine, Drake, and Diana </b> Basically, they are as cynical and evil as ever. There were brief points where I almost felt bad for Caine and Diana but not overly so. And Drake is crazy as ever. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I also highly doubt that Drake is dead. That was too easy.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380415031i/818963.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> All other characters </b> I like Edillio but I think he is a bit forgettable. He's in the book quite a bit yet I still haven't found him remarkable in any way. The same goes for Dekah for me.<br><br>I did like Brianna in this book and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ hope to see more between her and Jack. Although, Jack annoyed me by going back with Diana and Caine with how mean they were to him and how badly they treated him.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>Orc and Howard were pretty much the same to me as in Gone. Orc seems, maybe, like he's trying to be better overall though.<br><br>I'm not sure how to feel about Albert at this point. I really like him in Gone but it could go either way for me on him. We'll see how it plays out.<br><br>I thought Zil and Harry were crazy and I'm sure we haven't seen the last of them yet. In case Drake and Caine aren't enough, let's add these lunatics!<br><br>The three most intersting secondary characters to me were Duck, Hunter, and Brittney. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I felt so bad for Duck and Hunter! I really hope Duck is not dead and I feel bad that Hunter got exiled! I hope he is able to come back at some point.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I am really interested to see what role Brittney has in future books!<br><br>Petey also is having some crazy dreams! I feel like he's going to play a big key role towards the end of the series with something. I'm interested to find out what it is.<br><br>I am sure I am still forgetting characters but off the top of my head, that's all I can think of right now.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380415031i/818964.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="3917161294529792901" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText17097496028967729667" style="display:none">Definitely better than the first book, and there are a few things that occurred in this one that made the first book make more sense, relevant characters etc. <br />This book made me feel so frustrated but not in an entirely bad way, just because of how accurately it depicted what would happen if the situation were real. Some of the kids you want to congratulate and others you want to shake so badly to try and get it into their system that if they do that it'll have dire consequences. <br />I love how none of the 'heroes' are actually all that likable/lovable and have flaws but still pull through, and none of the 'evil' characters are black and white. <br />Sometimes I do have to remind myself they're all 15 and under, the way some of them act makes me be like oh my god you're far too young but at the same time I'm sure they'll have had to grow up in a sense very quickly.<br />Didn't absolutely love it but was definitely an enjoyable read and I'll be continuing the series. <br /></span>
